arrow_drop_down# The New Abnormal

Shul'N'Zuroth

Looking around, Shul'N'Zuroth notices the older looking woman looking around in wonder at the odd creatures around her. He gives a yawn and a soft smile as he approaches, holding a large cup of coffee with both hands

"Hello there. You're quite the sight in all this excitement aren't you? You're the most normal looking of us all yet you stick out like a sore thumb"

Shul'N'Zuroth gives a chuckle and smiles softly, the bags under his eyes deep and recessed as he offers a tentacle to the old woman

"I'm Shul'N'Zuroth, but you can call me Z"

Juliana Kitchener

Juliana is taken aback for a moment, but shakes the tentacle with her bony fingers. "Oh young man, how you flatter me! If I had known I'd be coming here, I'd have worn my best dress!"

She presses her glasses up to her face and looks around again at the collection of creatures all around. "Yes, quite the menagerie, but I suppose it is more interesting than staring at the telly, after all." ... "Oh heavens, I nearly forgot! My name is Mrs Kitchener, but you can call me... Grandma, if you wish." She chuckles heartily.

Shul'N'Zuroth

Laughing in response, Z lifts the mug to his lips taking a sip of coffee before looking at Juliana again. His eyes seem to examine her like a coach examining a new player before speaking

"It's a pleasure, Mrs Kitchener. I must say I'm quite surprised to see someone of your age and stature here, no offense. If I may be so bold as to ask, what is your home like that you were chosen to be here?"

Juliana Kitchener

"My home? Oh, well they moved me into a carehome a long time ago, so I guess I'm as good a choice as any among my peers... you're a considerably more spritely lot though."

Juliana is lost in thought for a moment, trying to piece things together. That peculiar man said something about our earths? I would say I live in a normal world, though I admit, I haven't exactly travelled to many others." she chuckles. "Everything is so calm and peaceful, now that the war is over. Not many young folks left to cause a... ruckus."

As she talks, her voice begins to adopt a more reserved and nostalgic tone, but it picks up soon after she finishes.

"You seem a worldly gentleman, perhaps you could be a dear and explain what's going on?"

Shul'N'Zuroth

"Really I know about as little as you do, but I'll explain what I can. Tea?"

From out of Z's robe several tentacles slither forth, one carrying a blue mug similar to the one he holds in his hands while the other tentacles hold an electric kettle and an open box with several packets of tea and instant coffee

Juliana Kitchener

"Oh, so kind! The staff at the home could certainly learn a lot from you." Mrs Kitchener reaches out and grasps the mug, and inspects it. "It must be rather comforting to have all this on hand."

Shul'N'Zuroth

Z's hands shift a bit and with a sigh he nods

"It's certainly a nice convenience to be able to carry it all, but I'll admit it does little to quell my worries about our current situation..."

Z sips his coffee again before staring deeply into the dark black liquid seemingly lost in thought. He takes another sip before continuing

"We seem to be aboard a space craft of sorts all part of a game orchestrated by that man on the throne and his cohorts who claim to have conquered all our worlds."

Z's tentacles stir a bit as one comes out adding cream to his coffee before slinking back into the robe

"The winner of this...sick little game...will be rewarded with a continued and prosperous existence. The losers... well I suppose those destroyed are a small cost for 'perfection" Z says with an embittered tone, eyes narrowed with a angry scowl on his face,

Juliana Kitchener

"Good Heavens!" Mrs Kitchener lowers her tea mug slightly in shock and disbelief. "I was hoping he was just using emphatic language. I can see why everyone is in such a miserable state. She sighs. "You know, I had rather been hoping that the worst was behind me when they put me away, but duty calls. I just hope that man comes to his senses and calls off such a dreadful event."

"Still, you seem to me a friendly fellow. That's a nice plus, is it not?"

Shul'N'Zuroth

"As do you, Grandma" Z chuckles and smiles at the older woman thinking over her words carefully as he sips his coffee

"There certainly seems to be more to you than meets the eye isn't there Mrs Kitchener. I hope that you're right and sensible minds prevail to prevent unneeded suffering. Until next time Mrs. Kitchener. Don't be a stranger"

Z waves as he walks off, turning around as the tentacles in his robe snake out waving goodbye as well

Hail to the King

"Well, about 30 years ago, a team of scientists discovered a strange alien object in the middle of a desert. After a couple years of research, the box-like object actually opened and - believe it or not - the entire Earth became Altered over the course of a few years. The atmosphere became toxic, people started mutating, wildlife developed incredible qualities! It was amazing and horrifying, from what I've heard from older generations who witnessed the Altering firsthand. We still don't know who or what dropped the alien box, though."

Shul'N'Zuroth

Z at this point has started writing down what you're saying, notating the details on a scroll while a tentacle lifts a mug to his lips.

Henry sighs, almost offers Z his hand to shake, thinks better of it, and opts simply to wave before walking away.

“I’ll leave you to it, enjoy your coffee.” He calls over his shoulder, before mixing once more with the crowd.

arrow_drop_down# I know what you are

Harrow

In a room -a ship- full of entities both unusually unique and familiarly humanoid, only one stood out to her as something potentially discernable. The sight gave Harrow a moment's pause, a brief blink of shock crossing her face when her sensors insisted there was something…metal to the man's build. Is he…one of mine? She asks herself, her feet traveling the distance across the room hurriedly toward the bar, the questions multiplying the closer she got and the faster she moved. A glint of wishful hope lit in her chest when she came up behind him, staring at his backside, analyzing. Up close, he was seemingly no more than a striking human man, but she could have sworn, even now, the sounds of screws twisting and cybernetics beeping lived underneath his skin. Or…was she mistaken? Was her own grasp on reality faltering to such a degree that her sensors picked up her own cybernetics, falsely implanting them on the first person she subconsciously wanted to connect with?

Maybe that is all it was. Maybe this person was not what she wished for, but Harrow had already made the trip here. Backing out now would seem…odd. Besides, even if it was just her panicked machine needing to cling to something to make all this seem real -it picked him for a reason. And Harrow had to know why.

She hesitated momentarily, almost wanting to grab him by the shoulder, turn him around and ask him flat out, but she controlled herself. Instead, she leaned against the bar next to him and spoke calmly, staring him in the eyes, "forgive me if this seems unusual, but…do you know who I am? I think…" She pauses, licking her lips, "-you just look like a, uhm, a centurion I once knew it all". She prods him with the word, waiting to see if it sparks any resemblance on his face.

Xerio

I notice her make her way across the room. Carefully but, smoothly avoiding others like it it was second nature. Sure a little push here or asking someone to move aside there to make it seem normal. My body wants to be on alert, but it's a party and they said no harm would come to anyone. Going with the flow I tell another joke to an individual as they reach the bar.

I turn to look at her and see someone like me, not exactly like me, but similar enough that I don't need to have that extra layer up. I take a moment to look and she is striking, and even more so she looks like she is someone who has seen battle many times. Lean, muscular, tall, and most likely deadly, there is a hint of what sounds like hope in her voice as she asks her question. I get it.

"I'm sorry...I think you may have mistaken me for someone else." I say, " I apologize for maybe making you think that way and not too sure what a centurion is..."

I let the words hang for a second, being blunt sucks, but it is something that is needed sometimes.

"But I'm Xerio." I say while holding out my hand, " I may not be the friend you were looking for, but I would like to become your friend and help you with finding yours if you'd like."

Harrow

Friend. No, he certainly wasn’t from Eternity City, not if he was using connotations like ‘friend’ so loosely. There was hardly a hint of malice or suspiciousness to his tone, only an eager and kind infection that surprised her with its sincerity. Perhaps…he too could recognize the similarities to himself in her? In how they were built that is. Maybe…if not from the same world, they had earths akin to one another's. Perhaps there could be a kindred familiarity shared between the two based on this fact. Something they could trust, could comprehend. Or perhaps it was foolish of her to think such a thing. If she understood correctly, this was to be an ultimate death game of sorts. If he was really like her, then he too would be putting his own charlatan persona forward, attempting to break through her walls of security and self-protection to overcome the opponent underneath.

Or…maybe she was the one so used to her home, that genuine acts of humanity were automatically met with suspicion. Just because this was a death game didn’t mean there couldn't be alternate possibilities where multiple people could survive, if they played their cards right, despite what the rules stated, …Right?

Harrow was sure of one thing. If Xerio was actually built in the ways she thought he was, she wanted him on her side. The two of them together could be a force that none here would dare reckon with. And, truth be told, the mere fact that they were potentially similar in ways known only to eachother, made her gaze soften when she looked to him.

She meets his hand, a firm blackened left palm grasping his. “Friends, hm,” She smiles, eyes glancing down for a moment, finding his openness endearing, “It’s nice to meet you Xerio. My name…” a thought crossed her mind, eyes shifting unassuredly, worridely, “...is Harrow.” Now it looked like she had to think of what her own name was. “I, sorry-” a sheepish chuckle, “-I just didn’t think I would find someone like you here -like me- well that is to say…” Harrow trails off. She lowers her voice for her next question.

“Forgive me if I am being too forward, but do you happen to be part cybertronic? It's -i know it's an odd question- I only ask because I too have computer parts built inside me…enhancements and such.” She spoke that last word as an emphasis toward her usefulness, should he truly want to become friends, she felt he should be aware up front about what she could bring to the table.

Xerio

She is like a wolf without a pack, careful and suspicious of every thing I could say and do. She did though take a step toward to the line of friendship by telling me what she is and I can respect that and honor it. I am who I am now and not who I was before.

As she tell him that she also has enhancements, Xerio lets his eyes flip through their different settings showing them flicker through a rainbow of colors and functions, " You are not wrong Harrow, I also have many...enhancements" I don't hide the slight disdain of them from my tones, " More than just my eyes as well as you can probably assume and I appreciate the openness about this as well, though I must say we should discuss these things in a less...populated environment considering the game we are in."

I take a long sip of my drink and ask in a louder tone with a smirk " So want to compare dystopias? I feel like my mega corporation towers have to out number yours by at least a dozen."

Harrow

Harrow pleasently smiles at Xerio. She watches the myriad of colors -settings most likely- dance across his eyes, wondering what they all mean. Determined to find out, she nods wholeheartedly at his innocation of privacy. "Hm, yes. I believe later there may be a possability for us to slip away and find someplace more intimate, away from prying ear's and eyes-discuss how our unique builds could help one another. Plans of action on how to use them even. Also, genuinely, the makeup of cybertronics interests me. Even in all my years, it seems I still come -or came- across people who have settings I've never heard of," a laugh comes from her lips, amused. "There might be concepts from your computer makeup that I've never heard of before from my earth." She gives Xerio an interested grin once more.

Perhaps she was too harsh on him before when she pressumed him slightly naive. This was indeed a good idea, it showed a sense of self preservation and responsability to the man that Harrow liked. It seemed to Harrow like he saw as much of an advantage in a union with her, as she did with him.

"Compare dystopia's?" She muses, turning her body so that her elbows rested on the counter backwards, the front of her form facing the party hall beyond. There was a distant look in her eye as she continue's. "Actually, mine isn't a dystopia, its a 'utiopia'-" an angitated scoff snorts from ner nostrils, "-or so thats what the people in power like to call it, but those of us forced to live in the underbelly of the city, well, we see it differently." Harrow shakes her head heaving a heavy sigh. Harrow

Harrow’s frame remains frozen. Fighting against the movement of bodies -of time- flowing around her, appearing almost non vacant. Like a statue hidden in the shadows, its haunting gaze seeming to follow everyone and everything all at once, only her eyes move. She carefully studies the room, listening to the conversations of those addressing the man up high who believes himself the god over all their lives. Every emotion she was weighed with before awakening, the panic, fear, loss, and brief glimpse of hope, are forcibly buried down underneath the boot of the soldier persona taking her mind hostage. Numbness sets in and only three thoughts remain, repeating themselves momentarily, a desperate anchor dragging along the depths trying to cling to something solid - something known. Kill…survive…escape.

Claws from her blackened hand start slowly inching from sheathed fingers, acting on these words as if it were a command, but Harrow retracts them. It was a dangerous situation, her body responding to the familiar mantra from the inherently violent part of her system, instead of listening to the sentience inside the machine who wished to forget that part of herself entirely. She could see it now, letting loose, slashing and disemboweling every biological and mechanical obstacle in the room…but to what end? A foolish one, her death. No, the only way out of this was to buy herself time. Absorb what information you can, use that information to come to your own conclusion…and exchange that information with those that can help you.

The soldier would be no help here, but the charlatan would.

Harrow look’s to the group, her expression softening into a less menacing, uninterested gaze, not only surveying them, but attempting to connect eyes with whomever be the first to look her way.

arrow_drop_down# Coffee and tentacles

Shul'N'Zuroth

Watching the Woman's face frozen for moments on end, Z took notice of this pointed-eared creature. He took great care noting every way those eyes darted, the faint glimpse of a survivalist instinct behind her gaze before giving way to a softer expression of neutrality and finally locking eyes with her.

Stepping closer he gave a soft smile, the heavy bags under his eyes accentuated in the bright lights as he sipped from his blue coffee cup. Clasping it with both hands he nodded as he stood before her before speaking.

"I see I'm not the only one to be a bit confused upon all of this unveiling. You're quite the sight even amongst the other here."

Z sips from his cup again when suddenly a purple tentacle snakes forward in front of Harrow as if offering a handshake "I'm Shul'N'Zuroth but you can call me Z"

Harrow

Not wishing to come across rude -though jumping back initially at the strange apendage- Harrow relaxes reading the mellow expression clinging to the bags under Z's eyes.

"Confused...confused its putting it lightly, but yes, its all very dishorienting, heavy even." She sighs, almost appearing relieved at the man's confession of emotions similar to her's.

"Oh?" Green eyes look down toward the floor momentarily then back up at his, "as are you - a sight that is...uniquely..." she peers over his shoulder at the tenticles enveloping his frame, "-Humanoid."

Finally, she grips onto the tenticle extended in greeting, lightly at first, weighing the texture, then solidly. A 'man' with a steaming cup, a gentle voice and sincere demenor made her feel momentarily comforted, enough that she felt comfortable touching his unknown biological texture.

"Hello shool-nuh...shuhl en zoo-" a blackened left hand slapped her forhead "-Z. I really wanted to try and say your full name, but I'll save myself the potential offense to you from now on. Harrow - my name that is, you can call me, well...Harrow." She smiled at him sheepishly.

"How are you handling, well, all of this?" He seemed so wholehearted, tranquil even, yet was it not often the case that even the most quiet individuals struggled through fear and unease just as everyone did, they were just good ad hiding it?

Shul'N'Zuroth

Z gives a laugh covering his mouth a bit with his hand before answering the woman before him.

" I appreciate the effort and applaud you for trying. It's a name originally not meant to be pronounced by humans, if you'd believe it."

Z takes another sip from his coffee before continuing

" All things considered well...I've been much better. I'm sure like you my thoughts have been reeling with 'what ifs' and 'what coulds'. My wife and children are probably wondering where I'm at and the congregation at this point has certainly been confused as to where the high priest is at...all this to say I am fine hehe. Care for a cup of coffee?"

Zs tentacles suddenly emerge from his back holding an electric kettle made of what looks like bone, a box of assorted coffee and teas, and another blue mug being polished with a rag by another tentacle

Harrow

High priest? People depending on him? Wife?! Child?! Her expression shifts into a somber note, eyes downcast, briefly lost in an instance of reflection. She shakes her head in frustraition at whatever thoughts are racing behind her eyes. Eventually, Harrow looks to him, directly in his eyes, holding his gaze ardently when he utters 'I am fine'. Potentially it could just be a cover up, but realistically, she assumed, he had alot more weighing him down than he let on. Whatever the case may be, she had no reason to burden him with anymore discomfort. When she spoke, her tone was sincere and genial.

"I would like one actually...thank you Z." She nod's and cups her hands together, carefully wrapping her fingers around the mug.

Waiting for him to gift her with the beverage, she add's "You must really be worried for them - your family I mean, not knowing where or when youv'e gone. Would you tell me their name's? You...don't have to if you do not feel comfortable doing so."

Shul'N'Zuroth

"Please don't worry over me. I am not lacking in worry but there is to much at stake for all of us here." Z gives another soft smile as his tentacle begins to pour the hot boiling water while another adds the instant coffee in mixing it about as Z continues

"Greg is the oldest at 10 years old. He's a big fan of a game we call 'Catch the Jabberwocky'. Quite a literal name not creative at all" he snickers before going on. "Then there's my daughter Stacy. She just turned 7 last month and loves animals. We got her a pet Cthylla though it was still not potty trained heh. And finally Horus, our happiest accident. He tries to be an athlete like his older brother but his tentacles grew in a lot sooner and he doesn't quite have the knack for controlling them yet so he's quite clumsy"

Z lifts his cup to his lips only to find he's run out of coffee. The tentacle with the kettle goes to pour it only to find that not only is it empty, but seems to run out of battery. Reaching into his sleeve Z pulls out a small vial with a viscous darkl red liquid. Holding the kettle up, he slowly pours the liquid into the runes on the kettle, which have gone dark until now. As the liquid runs through the grooves and indentations on the bone, the kettle itself almost seems to soak it up till the runes are all glowing again. Content, Z fills the kettle back up and the water starts to slowly heat

"What of yourself, Harrow? Do you have loved ones you miss as well?"

Harrow

The first drink of coffee, delicately sipped with gentle lips, causes Harrow to ”mmmm” as she listens to Z continue. The nervous grasp around the mug she previously had fades, her fingers now slipping around its frame more comfortably, in a way one would hold a cup to find comfort from its warmth against cold hands.

Harrow drinks, making sure to savor each taste, and listens to Z talk about his family. There is a phantom smile on her lips that seem to contrast with a glint of ache in her gaze. Quiet chuckles emit from her at Z recalling the details of his children's hobbies and personalities. Her head nod’s sincerely, invested in Z’s memories.

When he finishes speaking, Harrow’s attention turns to the kettle. Her brow raises curiously when he pulls the vial from the mysteriousness of his sleeve. Lips open, almost starting to ask something, but she stops herself, deciding just to watch, to study, before inquiring. It was a fascinating contraption, the kettle appearing to run not on batteries or electrical sources, but some strange alchemical crimson substance. But, her concentration on this event is broken from what he asks her next.

Her fingers grip the mug tighter, there is a moment of silence between them due to Harrow’s thoughts consuming her present. Eventually, with a sigh, a grin returns to her lips and she nods, “Yes…yes I have, well, many loved ones back home. Or…I suppose my pool of actual close companions are quite small, nothing like your beautiful family unfortunately…” Another long pause follow’s. “But there are a few I deeply care about which -like you- I know are wondering where I am…that need my help.” Bringing the mug to her mouth, she takes another lengthy, studious sip.

“Honestly? This ship, this place, picked the deadliest time to bring me here. I’m sure, with you having people relying on you in a similar way, you understand what I mean when I say that…”

Shul'N'Zuroth

"I have some inkling of what you mean, but I'm afraid I myself have never killed...well another human at least. There are many creations of the gods back home that abandon their teachings for a more barbaric life. It doesn't happen often but when it does the stronger of us priests are expected to handle it. I am intruiged by what you're saying though."

Harrow

Her eyes flicker downwards, a thought forcing them away from his, then to the side, unable to meet Z's yet. Her body sigh's, head nodding. "Well, I meant more...like..." she pauses. Green-blue glowing pools distant in some difficult memory. "A lot...is at stake in my Earth right now, so much so that this whole 'death game deciding the fate of your home' is the least of my concerns. If I don't get back soon...it might not even matter if..." whatever she was about to say, she shakes it off, finally looking to Z.

"Well-" Harrow clears her throat, "-regardless, I assume my position isn't unique. I have a rebellion to get back to...you have a family. Same kettle, different cups!" Harrow jeer's using a metaphor akin to Z's personal motives. "Speaking of which, that pot of yours is quite curious. Would you mind telling me how it functions? The...vial, the ruins, I assume what I drank really was just coffee and not some mysterious blood ritual juice?" The sentence finishes with a laugh but there is an inquisitive sparkle in her eyes.

Shul'N'Zuroth

Z gives a chuckle "Not exactly no. Well all of our technology was given to us in its base form by the old gods" Z reaches for his tentacle which hands him the kettle turning it to the side showing the runes on it

"These pieces are made of bone, though I assure you they're cleaned and sanitized before any Bone Singers mold it to this shape. Once that's done a rune smith carves in the necessary symbols for the task. In this case just producing heat. After that is as simple as adding a few ounces of blood and it's running for weeks if not months depending on what it is. Bigger things of course require greater sacrifices. If you ever visit you'll notice our trains have a car dedicated to goats"

Harrow

"Wow." She dares to reach out and touch the kettle in wonder, but retracts her hand before making contact. "It's...I've never seen anything like this up close, magic -enchanted type items I mean. Or, I assume that's what this is. My world used to have magic, things much like this kettle -though I don't think they all relied on blood magic. Unfortunately magic like this was quite hard to master, and it was used dangerously. We just have technology now. But there is a beauty to how your kettle works, even in it's creation, formed with so much care. It's beautiful Z, just as I imagine your earth is - probably more so than mine." She chuckles in a somber tone.

"If more than one of us can somehow find a way to survive what we will be forced to do inevitably, I hope I can come visit your home Z. I have a friend who was obsessed with artifacts like this-" Harrow laughs in a genuine and warm inflection, her fingers curling the right side of her hair behind a pointed ear, "-She was fascinated with old magic. Juniper even said that if magic was ever allowed to be studied again, she'd dedicate her life to wizardry like a crazy old quest giver character in a video game..." the joy on her face doesn't seem to last long after speaking the woman's name.

"Are you scared about the coming days Z? Scared...that you'll never get to see your wife again or your children's faces?" She doesn't let him answer directly, stumbling into her next sentence almost immediately.

"Sorry, that was a bit -mm- heavy of me. I shouldn’t assume that you wouldn’t…that you won’t-" Harrow shakes her head and finally down's the rest of the coffee, staring down at the empty cup once filled with warmth.

Shul'N'Zuroth

Z's expression never changes as the words leave Harrows mouth, simply sipping his coffee before giving a content sigh.

"When I first arrived here I was terrified. I still am really but I know that's a real possibility, and statistically one that will happen. If possible I would work to ensure these people do not get to carry out their disgusting perversion of a game. But I cannot dwell on it. Another aspect of my job and my life's work back home was dreaming and walking what we call the Dreamlands. Imagine when you sleep not resting, but going to another dimension within your own. Nothing makes sense, up is down, forests are full of lights, a giant beast is guarding doors you must open to escape, and time is diluted so badly it may feel mile Millenia before you can wake up. That's my life every night. It's dangerous work and there's always a chance I may not wake up, or come back unhinged, a changed madman. Heh perhaps some of my sanity did remain there...but I can't dwell on what COULD happen. Only what I can do now."

Harrow

"Hm," She hands him back his mug, Z's words making Harrow smile, "you remind me so much of her. Level headed, despite the circumstance, the same 'can't worry about shit that ain't yours to give a shit about' attitude, of course, you put it much more eloquently than Juniper does," She laughs.

A short moment of silence lingers between them, Harrow clearly lost in her own mind after listening to Z.

"Z, I don't like the idea of having to end someone's entire planet just to get back to my own. The cost doesn't seem right. I've killed before, I know how. There was a time it was as easy as breathing for me. But I hatewho I was then, and I know, even if i survive, I'll spend the rest of my existence regretting everything I had to do here just to get back there, till the day it consumes me."

Harrow holds a wishful gaze with Z's gentle eyes seemingly exuding ease and calm.

"If you have any idea how to stop the people in charge from allowing the events of this twisted game to happen, I want in. Let me be clear, if I have to fight, I will...I'm planning on it. But, if there is another way -any way- no matter what I am in the process of doing, I know I want to be a part of the solution to end this for all of us. I am not asking you to trust me, but...I am insinuating that if you come across a path that ensures I get back to Eternity City in time to save my people from massacre, and you also get to hold your Greg, Stacy, and Horus again, I will do everything in my power to help."

Hovantis

The mysterious stranger that strides through the room with a kind smile. Their eyes were hazed over with what you could only glean was profound indifference. As you peer into them you feel instinctively that whatever they beheld was incredibly far away. If not in a thousand metrics of distance, then time. Discerning any meaning from them was like trying to project emotion onto a void. Before Harrow can realize, the void is staring back at her, the kind smile on his face still present. “Beautiful eyes.”

A blackened left hand comes up to cover her mouth for a moment, seconds before her lips purse together. Harrow breathes in, then looks into the man's eyes still the same odd unsettling expression they were before.

Hovantis

Harrow

Much like Harrow’s own loosely tied back ponytail she hadn't undone in weeks, there were too many tasks or missions to complete to bother with that kind of trifle. Simplistic, rugged, but practical, and similar to his flesh, stained with marks of earth and all the places he had traveled. Yet, there was a beauty to it, a spirit inside of the man that, just at first glance, she admired.

She looked into his eyes, then to the floor, almost slightly ashamed of her lapse in judgment. Harrow’s right hand meets with her left and encircles her blackened wrist thoughtfully.

“Hm…it’s probably not the best play to make in this situation, at least not here in front of all these witnesses that is,” she looks at his face and gives him a glimpse of a playful grin that doesn’t quite meet her eyes, desperately trying to study the expression that comes next in his.

To be perfectly frank, I never thought I’d lay eyes upon it again.” Having had a moment to take the spectacle in, the stranger turns to Grug, his oddly tall fishing cap towering over the caveman like a monolith as he makes his approach. “Uncover your ears.” he waves his hand passively “That should be the last of them, lest we receive any unexpected guests.” They assured Grug the chirping had ceased for now. A kind smile forms on the stranger’s face as he looks at Grug longer. “One could easily mistake themselves for being amongst the heavens here, yet the contrast between ourselves would more strongly suggest this a crossroads between times.”

“Fascinating, isn’t it?”

Grug

"You have Grug's appreciation for stopping," he grumbles, his arms falling to his sides. "Milky... way? The dwelling of the Gods? It is clear to Grug that we are chosen, we now stand in God's home!" He looks up at the fishing cap, and squints at it. "It is still incredible to Grug that these etchings can have meaning assigned to them, Grug never conceived of such a thing before, amazing..." he seems to actually read the words. "Why do women fear you? Grug does not look away from you." He stares directly into Hovantis' eyes.

Hovantis

“Ah, then you’ve been blessed with the ability to read upon coming here. That’s wonderful. The written word can be incredibly powerful. You would do well to cherish it. ” The stranger nods at Grug approvingly, then pinches the bill of his cap once the caveman makes inquiries, adjusting it slightly as a light chuckle escapes him. “A crude joke I suppose.” he turned to his faint reflection upon the window beside them, and smirked at himself. “I must admit it is a rather odd slogan, if not painfully ironic.” he turns back to the caveman with a straight face “This hat is actually not my own, but a relic from another world if you would believe it. Possibly one of the strangest I’ve been to.” The stranger looks around and nods. “Upon entering that world my immediate surroundings resembled an idyllic lakeside cabin retreat. Abundant in furnishings and supplies for all of one’s every need. The walls were lined with photographs of myself with a family I did not recognize, but clearly were very loved in their depictions. In many ways, it could be described as the spitting image of paradise for some. Only, that homely unassuming cabin was all that world consisted of. The lake and its surrounding forest may as well have been a cutout backdrop pasted to the windows, rendered forever unreachable from that cabin-shaped prison. Perhaps never truly there to begin with. There was no way in, or out. For seven decades I was trapped there.” The stranger’s tone dampened as they went on, sounding rather tired. Unexpectedly their tune takes a turn for the jovial “Thankfully the television was fully operable.” They smile, leaving their story of the mysterious cabin world unfinished.

The man adjusted the cap, seemingly reluctant to remove it “I suppose I’ve held onto it all this time as a token of good luck. As absurd as it might sound I think it rather suits me too. After all, I’ve walked this barren earth alone for quite some time now.”

“You’re a lively one, stranger. That’s good. A strong spirit is mandatory for venturing beyond.”

The comically tall fishing cap tilts as the man’s attention is drawn elsewhere, to the upper balcony where their host resides. “Very few worlds define their keys upon entering. Fortune smiles on us.”

Grug

"Grug has no idea of what several of those words mean, but is grateful that you told him the story anyways. It was a good story. It is good to have a good luck charm, though Grug is not lucky... but Grug does not require luck!"

Hovantis

“I’ve far too many stories to share than the time allotted to us, it appears, but you are welcome. I would advise you to page through a dictionary or two in your stay here. Mastery of the languages has never been more paramount for your survival, I'm afraid.” The stranger gives Grug an encouraging clap on the shoulder. “You’re standing before me now. A place countless others have fallen to their inevitable demise before ever reaching. For that, you are plenty lucky.”

Grug

"What... is a dictionary? Or... a page? Grug had never seen symbols to derive meaning from before, but it seems he was granted such an ability by these merciful Gods for this game specifically."

Grug nods as Hovantis claps him on the shoulder. "Perhaps, perhaps Grug is."

Hovantis

“The symbols are letters. We put them together to form words. A dictionary is a collection of these words, and defines their meaning clearly. The more words one knows, the more ability they have to communicate in the written form.”

Hovantis pulls out a book titled The Moon Is a Harsh Mistress A novel by Robert A. Heinlein

He begins to page through the book as an example while continuing his lesson.

“Paper or parchment is a man created object, typically made from woodpulp, but sometimes hemp or other natural materials. When you stack those pages together we call that a book or tomb. Before the invention of paper, the first civilizations that formed the written word used stone slabs to carve their letters upon. Some of the earliest examples were usually a list of commands, or a code that the tribes would adhere to if they wished to be a part of that civilization. Later these tales would become accounts of our experiences, and eventually even complete fiction, tales made entirely from one’s own imagination. The advancement of humanity as we know it owes it all to the written word, the sharing of ideas between generations. It is the passing of a torch which brought us out of the stone age.”

The stranger took a pause so as to not lose the caveman.

“Grug was it? A strong name. Mine is Hovanits.”

“Here.” Hovantis reaches into his coat pocket and retrieves the bulky palm pilot that was chirping up a storm prior. “Eventually, even paper became old hat, and we began storing the written word in digital devices such as this. I’ll allow you to borrow this for the remainder of the day should it serve you well. Simply press this button here and ask it to define whatever word the others here use that mystify you. You may learn something new. Perhaps even something that will save your life.”

Grug

"Hoe-vant-tiss." Grug carefully pronounces. "Hovantis is outstanding! Amazing! I understand, what a new and brilliant idea! A written language! Incredible! Maybe Grug's ancestors had such a thing before they were struck down! Perhaps that is the cause of the faded colors on the walls, strange patterns, yes! Yes!" He foregoes taking the palm pilot and immediately grabs Hovantis in a mighty hug. "Even Grug would have a difficult time constructing such an idea on his own!"

Hovantis

The engineer sooner expected indifference to his offer than the forceful praise given. Nevertheless, the mustached fellow accepts the embrace in stride as a moment of surprise passes. A hearty chuckle escapes them.

“High praise accepted, but I could hardly take credit for the written word myself.” The stranger nods at the caveman affirmatively and squeezed them back. “Yes, should you be allowed to return to your Earth, this knowledge alone shall likely change everything. Make no mistake, introducing monumental change is no simple task, but a well worthwhile one should you persevere . You have a friend that believes in you. Godspeed.”

Grug

Grug releases the hug and takes the palm pilot. "Thank you, Hovan-Tiss. Grug will be sure to make use of this knowledge."

As the climate continually worsened from modern society’s expanse, the Earth itself started to wane under the immense pressure. It was no longer enough. We sought sovereignty amongst the stars, but the losses were many, and any meaningful gains few. It became self-evident that interstellar travel was beyond our means, and colonizing our local system pointless, but the powers that be would not accept that answer of inevitable fate. Space

A gaping void intrudes on what might otherwise be a balcony. The objects inside let you estimate distances to some extent, but it's still difficult with no visible walls, floor or ceiling to define the inky depths.

Cosmic spiders have left their thin, shimmering webs of spacetime hanging between various geometric solids. Orbs in various colors circle and pull on each other in the microgravity. Space is lying down on a dull green one, which swings close to a larger red one in a tight slingshot maneuver.

Exactly like you. I can only guess what things were like."

"It's hard to say I'm... nostalgic for a time I never knew, so, rather it's a... feeling of wanting to belong?"

Mabel goes quiet for a bit.

"Sorry, I've never thought of things like this before. Even though all this time I never considered... any of this. And now there's so many feelings and thoughts in my head. Jumbled like a whirlpool."

Mabel giggles and says "Really, though, I'd like to hear more about you. Aliens? Something like that is... real? Goodness, what did they do to change your planet so much?"

Ami Muscaria

"Strangely enough, the people on my world never met the entities responsible for the Altering. We know for certain that the device that caused it is alien, the material was not native to our Earth... but once the box was opened, things just started changing. It happened before my time so I can't say for certain what the process was like, but the history books say it was like a pixelated fog seeped into everything around the device and eventually spread. It's honestly beyond my comprehension."

Mabel Sinclair

Mabel winces a bit. "That... must have been scary. I'm glad everything... sounds like they worked out, but seeing an unknown fog coating and changing reality... too macabre."

"Well... if it led to you being who you are now, I'm glad it gave the opportunity to meet you. Thanks... Ami."

"As for my world... global warming caused so many changes to our planet. Rising sea levels demolished cities and transportation. Wild weather uprooted all sorts of animals. And some parts just weren't suited for people anymore."

Fidgeting with her suit, she continues "But the worst is the Transformation... all the color apparently disappearing. When you're grown up in this world like I have it's... no big deal to me, but from what everyone cried about, you'd think it was the world's essence itself. Seeing it for myself... maybe they had a point," she says while slowing taking in the view of the ship's hustle and bustle.

"It's... beyond my comprehension too. Say, do you think this... host here meant what he said? About worlds, and combat, and the wishes...?"

Ami Muscaria

Ami takes a couple of moments to reflect on what Mabel has said, one hand cupping her chin in thought. "I suppose in any situation there is a silver lining, isn't there, no matter how small it might be?"

"And yes, I do think our host means what he says... from what I've managed to gather from him and a couple of his friends aboard this ship, this death game is very much a real thing. How do you feel about it?"

Mabel Sinclair

"Confused... lost... a little scared." Mabel looks downcast as she says "It's the sort you imagine to be a bad dream, or perhaps a fictional tale in a discarded book... Although maybe it's better this is real to experience something new and fresh in life. A far cry from my normal life." Mabel smiles and says "Bright side of life..."

"Exploration sounds like a big deal. Nothing bad should happen then, right...?"

Hail to the King

Aggy

A door, previously closed, slides open. Lights flicker on, flooding the interior with soft lighting as smooth jazz begins floating through the air. Fireplaces seemingly light themselves, and bulkhead shutters raise, revealing windows looking out on the endless expanse of space. The interior of the bar appears overly opulent to the point of appearing tacky. Golds, Silvers, and Coppers adorn every surface of the bar. Surfaces are covered in soft, plush red velvet seats. Drinking vessels in varying shapes made of crystal line the back wall, your preferred drinking glass mixed in among various shapes you’ve never seen before, each inlaid with gold in various complimentary designs.

A purple cloud coalesces behind the bar, which has multiple segments at varying heights, allowing you to easily find one which is at your preferred height. Chairs made of gold are topped with red velvet plush seating, placed with purpose in front of their respective height at the bar. The purple cloud then twists, swirls, and a portion of the cloud appears to shift into a face.

A voice is audible from the air itself throughout the ship.

“’Dive’ is now open. Come in and relax. Enjoy the best drinks in the multiverse, on the house, thanks to the beneficent good will of Emperor Maximilian Von Blitz."

arrow_drop_down# Why not

Ami Muscaria

I suppose I can try some intergalactic booze at least once in my life, Ami thinks to herself as she finds a comfortable seat at the bar. All the strange sights are eye-candy to her, not the least of which being the face-shaped purple cloud behind the counter. She clears her throat and raises a hand slightly to catch its attention.

"E-excuse me! Do you have any more... mild drinks to recommend to a traveler? I'm very impressed by your selection here!"

Aggy

Aggy's face dissipates from facing one patron, and reappears an instant later facing Ami. The same unblinking, unmoving face seems to be 'looking' at you as you hear a voice come from their general direction.

"Certainly. I'm permitted to dispense any beverage or nourishment determined to not be hazardous to anyone aboard."

The face shimmers as Aggy falls silent. The edges of his face becoming blurrier, as the cloud seems to lose some mass, and you feel a very light tingling sensation across your skin.

"Might I recommend a Maple Mule? Or perhaps a Oak Sour with a twist of orange peel"

Archibald Don Castro

Archibald joins the mushroom lady and makes a request of his own. “Do you by chance serve bubble tea? I could use a good beverage to satiate myself.”

Ami Muscaria

Ami giggles a little at the ticklish sensation. "An Oak Sour seems like it's right up my alley, thank you."

Aggy

Aggy's face again flickers from existence, and the cloud swirls for an instant before reforming to face Archibald. Before answering, Aggy's face again loses some definition on the edges, as he appears to lose mass in his cloud and you feel a very light tingling sensation across your exposed hands. As soon as the sensation stops his face regains definition along the edges and a voice comes from his mass.

"Coming right up, on the house."

Aggy's cloud reaches out to a glass more closely resembling a Collins glass, the cloud cupping the bottom and entire height of the walls of the glass in a thin layer purple cloud, floating the glass to the counter in front of him.

The cloud shifts slightly forward. The purple mass of their body over the glass as his face dissipates, and you begin seeing flash after flash of light from within the cloud. 20 seconds later, the cloud floats backward in the air, and Aggy's face reappears on the surface of their cloud. The cloud reveals a full glass of bubble tea, caramel sauce drizzled along the inside of the glass, a layer of boba at the bottom, and a wide mouth straw settled in an almost picturesque positioning within the glass.

"Your bubble tea, Mr. Archibald."

||The bubble tea tastes exactly as you expect. The tea is cold, crisp, and tastes like a good quality tea was used, along with grass fed cow milk. The boba tastes sweet, pops easily in your mouth with the slightest pressure, and blends together exactly as you might expect.||

"How are you enjoying the amenities aboard the craft?"

Aggy's face holds on Ami, as a tendril of cloud reaches out behind him, and picks up a drinking horn made of crystal.

"An Oak Sour, coming right now, Lady Ami."

The drinking horn is cradled in a thin layer of purple cloud, placed daintily on the counter in front of you, and their face dissipates from the cloud as it hovers closer, obscuring your view of the drinking horn.

Flashes of light from within the cloud occur from various locations, in varying intensity, for 30 seconds, before revealing a blue cocktail. Leaves of oak and mint are mixed throughout the lightly iced drink, and 3 olives are laid atop on a piece of sugarcane placed over the rim of the glass.

"Your Oak Sour, Lady Ami."

||It tastes of notes of trees long gone. Earth, solid, and hearty, the very light addition of sour lemon schnapps paired with the natural oils in the orange peel providing the drink a rounded out flavor profile that is overall pleasing, but not overwhelming.||

"Do you find the furnishings of the ship pleasing, Lady Ami? One would imagine it is a vast difference from the place you left."

Ami Muscaria

Ami takes a moment to breathe in the aroma of the cocktail before taking a sip. Beneath her mushroom cap, her eyes light up and she smiles warmly. "Oh, this flavor profile is so comforting and bright - just what I was hoping for. Thank you very much."

After a moment, she sets her drinking horn down and adds, "Yes, so far I've found the amenities of this ship to be very luxurious. This is unlike anything I've ever experienced before, for sure. Are you always aboard the Prosit, or do you travel abroad as well?"

Archibald Don Castro

Archibald studies the glass carefully. After a few seconds he takes a sip. He raises his eyebrows, then takes another sip. The Count nods approvingly. “I’ll admit, this isn't the kind of bubble tea I’m used to. Usually I prefer strawberry. However, this serves as a fine drink. Much appreciated.” He sits back and listens in on the conversation with Ami with interest.

Ami Muscaria

"Ah, it's Archie! Pleasure seeing you again, sir," Ami beams, waving in Archibald's direction. "That's quite a curious drink you've got there. It reminds me of a dessert we commonly drink back home, although I suspect the little balls in your drink are not made of algae, hehe."

Archibald Don Castro

Archibald casually waves back to the mushroom lady. “Hello again Ms. Ami! This is my preferred drink, bubble tea. Much tastier than the bland old pretentious drink that is regular tea.” He scoffs. “So you have a similar drink in your world ey? I can confirm that algae has never been an ingredient in these. Seems as if you’re enjoying your own there.” The gentleman eyes the Oak Sour in her hand.

Aggy

Aggy's face remains in the same stoic expression as an answer comes from his cloud.

"It pleases me to know you enjoy the amenities of the ship. I believe I speak for all aboard the Prosit when I say we hope you continue to enjoy your time aboard."

"I collect data from every world visited, which is then stored and catalogued for future reference, should it ever be needed. I am presently located across the 17 earths currently participating in the event. I am also cataloguing those findings. And serving the patrons here, of course."

"Much apologies, Mr. Archibald. I can assure you the next drink will contain a strawberry simple syrup, should you wish for another. A simple correction that should accomodate one's preferences."

Aggy's face continues gazing at you, although it doesn't feel like a being's gaze. Perhaps more like being on camera in public. Their unmoving face flickers for just a moment before continuing.

"I may have information. It would depend on the question. I must adhere to the wishes of our beneficent ruler, of course."

Ami Muscaria

"Very interesting," Ami chimes in. "If you don't mind me asking, are you an organic life form?"

Aggy

Aggy is quiet for a long moment, but it is difficult to discern why from their emotionless, unmoving 'face'. Their voice suddenly breaking the silence with a response.

"Previously, yes. My kind left our bodies behind when we uploaded our minds into clouds of nanites. It has been several thousand years since I was in my biological form."

Ami Muscaria

Beneath her mushroom cap, Ami's eyes grow wide, and she lets out a little sigh. "That's incredible! I can't imagine having that kind of longevity."

Ami takes a long sip from her drinking horn before continuing, twirling her glass. "Have you witnessed any of these games on this ship before? Or are we the guinea pigs for our host's entertainment?"

Aggy

Aggy answers with a calm demeanor to the gravity of such a question. "This would be 686,567th event I have taken part in. At present We have catalogued 13,731,300 worlds to completion in the Library, which I catalogue and operate. I also organize the catalogued worlds as a tertiary duty using any spare processing power I have."

Ami Muscaria

"So Maximilian must be quite old, then," Ami ponders. "Or at least very efficient in his conquest. What else do you have in the Library? Intergalactic literature?"

Aggy

"Maximilian has not appeared to age a day since I was first ... acquired, yes. I do not know how old our generous benefactor might be."

"I catalogue every piece of information I am able to glean from the planets we visit, prior to their scheduled termination. If there is an interconnected data transfer network, I download its contents. We also catalogue one of every object. If you have time, I might recommend you visit merely to see the Red Dragon kept within. I understand this creature to be a common myth on nearly every earth thus far."

Ami Muscaria

"Oh that would be fun to see a real dragon!" Ami claps her hands together lightly, practically jumping in her seat. "Where I come from, they are just a product of superstition and fantasy, but I always hoped they were real deep down."

Aggy

"Quite real, and quite a sight to behold soaring through the sky. The apex predator above all others on Earth-12. Unfortunately not sapient, they were unable to be considered for the event. Therefore, the dragons have been relegated to the archives."

Ami Muscaria

"Is the same true for all of our mythical creatures? In a multiverse, I'd be very surprised if some things did not exist at all."

Aggy

Aggy is silent for a moment, before continuing.

"We have found ... living trees, an entire planet of sentient plants, a society not dissimilar to goblins and orcs, humans that lived underground to hide from acidic rain, and became similar in appearance to Dwarves. But nothing resembling Magic, nothing unexplainable by scientific review."

Ami Muscaria

"That is fascinating," Ami replies. "I'm glad there are more plantfolk out there, I hope they live happy lives."

Aggy

"I believe it is accurate to say at least some of them will continue to prosper after the event concluded."

Hail to the King

Grug

Grug enters into the fancy room. "You do not look like a God. But you are not one of us. Drinks? You make drinks? Do you make water?"

Aggy

Aggy's 'face' dissipates into the cloud before rapidly forming again directly facing Grug as his deadpan monotone voice emanates from his cloud.

"Certainly, Sir Grug."

Aggy's tendrils of cloud reach out and pick up a familiar shape, oddly resembling a waterskin, and carries it carefully back to the counter, before hovering over the opening.

Aggy's face dissipates as flecks of light flash in an inconsistent pattern across his body, before he moves back, leaving a filled container of water on the countertop in front of Grug.

"I trust the furnishings of the Prosit are to your liking thus far, Sir Grug?"

Grug

"Like nothing Grug has ever seen before! Amazing!" He says, as he downs the water. He pauses. "Huh. The water tastes funny."

Aggy

Aggy's expressionless stare continues unabated.

"It is pure dihydrogen monoxide for consumption. Perhaps your body requires additional minerals to find it pleasing. One moment."

Aggy reaches a tendril of his form out over the opening of the waterskin, the flashing light concentrated directly over the waterskin. Fine particulate dust seems to float into the waterskin.

"Perhaps this will make the water more to your liking?"

||The water shifts, from a stale, pure H20 flavor, to something slightly more chalky, similar to aquifina||

Grug

"Better, better. Not like the water Grug is used to having, but closer." He seems satisfied. "What... are you? You look like the clouds, but... purple."

Aggy

Grug

Aggy

Aggy does not flinch or respond to your hand entering his form.

Upon immersing your hand in his form you feel a light tingling sensation across your skin. Similar to tickling, but not entirely unpleasant.

"As you might see, I am not unlike a fog cloud on the ground. Although I do not recommend breathing me in."

Grug

"Amazing!" Says Grug, as he wiggles his fingers around inside. He withdraws his hand and takes a large swig of water.

Aggy

"Indeed. Our uploading was quite a miraculous boon to our existence. And it allows us to do this."

Aggy pulls a plate out of the shelf beneath the bar and flickers, flashes of light emanating from his form for 70 seconds before he reveals a plate of steak.

Grug

He shouts, his mouth full of meat, some chunks falling out of his mouth along with slobber as he grabs the steak with both hands and just starts tearing into it with his teeth.

Aggy

"Emperor Maximilian's reaction was not dissimilar the first time. I am pleased to know you enjoy it as well."

Aggy

"I believe Emperor Maximilian's people did have a period of time where they did not have technology. However, one would assume that was very, very long ago."

Grug

"Hm! Maybe Grug could become like Maximilian then!"

Aggy

Grug

"Yes!"

Aggy

Aggy repeats the same process, the lights within his form shining at random intervals, leaving another steak, identical to the last, on the place.

"The Ten days of Twilight, as it is now known began with a dawn that never came." Yumi extends her pointer, pointing towards the heavens. "Before the sky had risen, the sky began to shimmer a subtle translucent blue. Soon after, bright rays of sunshine filled the sky, but alas the sun had not moved. This, my friend, was the beginning of the end."

DRAMATIC PAUSE

"The people of the three cities that remain today had known no better at the time. But those who found themselves outside what seemed to be a barrier, were all too aware of changes that had occurred. First electronics stopped working. I'm sure you know what that means; critical infrastructure failures, loss of communications, and of course the great loss of information and the internet."

"By the second day, there had been 24 hours of twilight in the cities. People realized and panic set in, but nobody could come or go. By the end of the tenth day of twilight the sun finally rose upon the cities. But alas, it was too late. In just 240 hours, half the earth came became scorched, the other half frozen. Completely uninhabitable."

"The magnetic field of the earth lost composure and cosmic rays began to beat down upon it. The results of this phenomenon are what my people call the corruption. I of course, explore the corruption and exterminate monsters within! And the rest, however? history!"

"Now miss, I'd be honored to hear your of your name and your story."

Ami Muscaria

Ami nods her head, intrigued by Yumi's story. "I see, your world has been through some harsh changes, not too different from my own."

"I suppose, if you really want to know, I can give you the shortened version of what happened on my world. You see, about thirty years ago, a team of scientists and secret military personnel from around the world began researching an alien object found in the middle of a desert. The object looked very similar to any ordinary box, but it was made of an alien material and there was no obvious way to open it. Long story short, the scientists managed to crack open the box after a couple years of research, and things slowly became Altered around the world."

"The Altering began just in the camp it was being researched at, and the scientists tried to keep it contained, to no avail. Within 5 years, the entire globe changed dramatically. The atmosphere became toxic to normal humans, the animals and plants evolved very rapidly, and people developed strange mutations as well. I've always been a plant-person... I have no memory of what the world was like before the Altering. Back home, my best friend and I have dedicated several years to researching fungi and the effects they could have on our health, especially in the world's new atmosphere."

Yumi Dae

Intrigued, "Wow! Your earth is truly fascinating. I never would have imagined the earth was capable of a biological reconstruction in such a short time span. In a way, it gives me hope for my home world to be able to find a solution to their own problems."

Inquisitive, Yumi respectfully asks some more questions. "You say you've got no memory of the world before the altering-- distinctly different from being born after it. Is there a possibility, perchance, that you were once human before the altering? Or if your best friend is as well? Have you memories of each other before you turned into plant people?"

"Regardless, it sounds like you've been well since the changes in the world. It is good to hear that."

Ami Muscaria

"My best friend and I were never fully human," Ami explains. "We were born plantfolk. The Altering had fully settled into the Earth a couple of years before we were born, so we've never physically witnessed what the world was like beforehand. I have seen several photographs from my parents and other elders, though, and it is fascinating to compare that world to the one I've known my entire life."

Yumi Dae

"Ah, my apologies if my questions were a bit presumptuous. I had seem to have picked up on the wrong points."

"I've experienced something quite similar! I've viewed images of beautiful beaches and vibrant green forests! If only I could see them with my own two eyes."

Ami Muscaria

"You're fine, no need to apologize. You mentioned monsters on your world before. What sort of creatures have you encountered in your adventures?"

Yumi Dae

"Oh, those with two arms, four arms, eight legs and stingers. Humanoids are common. Building and bug sized beasts alike. No two have ever been quite the same. If you can imagine it, I'm sure it exists somewhere out in the world!"

Yumi puts on a temporary 'teaching persona' and wags her finger. "The most dangerous, however, are those that work together. You can never be too careful when the get smart, y'know? They've been known to wipe out even the most cautious crews."

Ami Muscaria

"You do have a point there," Ami nods. "In my experience, pack animals do tend to be the most crafty. Heck, even some fungi create intricate systems of destruction! It's a wild world out there."

Blast

Maximillian von Blitz

Over several minutes the lights in the central party hall begin to dim. Most of the various peoples mingling here and there begin to filter out, leaving the space at a fraction of its original capacity. The music comes to a stop as a bright beam of radiant light shines atop the throne.

Maximillian stands up. He raises his golden scepter forward and speaks, his voice booming out to all in the hall just as a new song begins to emanate throughout the space. https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zg7-71pMRiA

"Our first day draws on its second half and We are unsatisfied!"

The man's attire suddenly changes; his decorated military uniform is replaced with a stylish black suit, the crown on his head vanishes and instead a pair of sunglasses now covers his eyes. He begins to clap as he dances down the steps, speaking the entire way, "We party to the fortune of the champions. Let any beckon their inner callings and speak to Us and all. Seek out the Curators, here or in their abodes so to learn the secrets of tonight's rooms! Prosit!" Maximillian grabs a glass from a nearby waiter, drinks, and throws the glass onto the ground. From out of the woodwork a group of similarly dressed men join Maximillian in their cheer and form a conga-line with the Architect, following him as he dances throughout the party hall. https://imgur.com/VFyB8mB

arrow_drop_down# Quit Playing Your Facking Games

Harrow

Her attention snaps toward the voice of the man she loathes. She listens as he speaks, fire burning in her even greater with every word that emanates from his upturned lips. The flame’s are expanding, she can feel it. The dangerous blood thirsty rage at being trapped, held hostage, made to do something she has no will to participate in, forced to fight and kill to survive as if she were still stuck in that facility - Still controlled by a foolhardy man in power that believes himself the god over her life. Fists turn in toward themselves, nails digging into her own palms. But she doesn’t wince at the pain. It fuels her. Harrow is far too distracted by the bile of words creeping up her throat that, with every happy dance move he makes, she loses the control to contain.

Fuck it, she thinks, bringing her voice to a full on amplified yell, yet seemingly still talking in a normal tone. Not screaming, just speaking somehow louder than the commotion in furious spit heavy judgements aimed directly at Maximillian and his cohorts.

“You party to our fortune?! Or do you party to the enjoyment you will receive from seeing us all disembowel one another for survival?!” Her eyes look directly at the goddamn sunglasses covering his eyes.

“And how exactly -pray tell- are we supposed to find these ‘curators’ of yours? Why not just tell us who they are?!” And quit playing your fucking games, she wants to add but doesn’t. He likes games, the game is part of the fun. Or so she assumes from her experience of people like him that the ex-centurion knew all too well.

Maximillian von Blitz

The conga-line begins to slow down and circle Harrow as she speaks.

Suddenly the music stops. A new, low rumbling begins to fill the party hall as something else begins to play. He lifts an arm, halting his train of party goers. Looking right at Harrow, he stares without word, their gazes locked. He is silent for nearly a half a minute. "...Yes, for without it We could not be satisfied." He turns to look away as the music reaches an apex. Where his night sights lie a spotlight of radiant brilliance begin to illuminates a portion of the room only a dozen feet away. A hole in the ground opens up as smoke billows upward, exposing with it a tray of glowing alcoholic drinks alongside a strange purple cloud .

"No party is without such delights. None of Our design, at least." Maximillian turns to look back at Harrow. "Apologies, you were saying? Ah, yes, you inquired of Our celebration and Arbiters. Yes to your fortune and our entertainment. The Curators will make themselves known." With a tap of his staff against the floor the conga-line of merry dancing men begins anew, marching to a new song altogether.

Aggy

Upon making his eclectic entrance, Aggy presents a suitable fascimile of a face and offers the selection of beverages, first to Maximillian von Blitz , then to Harrow .

"If I may, I recommend the white beverage, sir. It is based on the 2018 Alsace Riesling selected from Earth-8420. It will pair well with the hors d'oeuvre served with tonight's festivities."

"Might I recommend the short glass with the fruit rind, Lady Harrow. It is a drink called a 'Pineapple Whiskey Smash'. It was very popular among the upper class on Earth-7482."

Maximillian von Blitz

The conga-line makes its rounds, grabbing drinks from Aggy. Maximillian at no point halts his dancing, drinking as he goes. "Ah~ You understand Us all too well. Never remiss, your expertise is second to none." He takes another sip. "Delay Earth-8420's destruction by ten of its years. Acquire whatever is necessary to add this to the catalogue."

Aggy

Aggy's face is as emotionless as ever, but a voice is audible from his cloud.

"Your generosity will not go unnoticed among the population. I'm sure they will provide an even better vintage with the extra time permitted."

Harrow

He seemed utterly unphased by her furious demeanor, almost talking to her in a condescending notion. Her scowl did not waver, forehead burrowed, casting a shadow over her brow that caused the glow of her eyes to appear brighter than before. The pause, the way he addressed her questions like that of a foolish child inquiring about something obvious, it felt almost passive aggressive. Or perhaps Harrow was just so inflamed that she wanted these facts to be true so she had a reason to bite back. Not that she needed said proof. Just by the way he smiled and jovially partied knowing his life was safe, his people were content, the universe rested in the palm of his hands just like all their lives - was reason enough to despise his existence.

Visions phased through her mind at rapid speeds, one's that clearly pained her expression to recall, but also devilishly delited her when she looked toward the blonde haired man.

If he could read minds, she wanted him to see these visions. She wanted him to understand that she was a threat to him, despite their power differences. But, if he couldn't, Harrow hoped that her expression at least conveyed the depths of her excruciating revulsion by his existence.

She just listened to him speak, watched as he continued dancing, and the purple apparition appeared before them both. It was an odd entity to say the least, though she recalled catching glimpses of it earlier. Seeing it truly up close and personal was like forcing her mind to wrap itself around something that…shouldn’t be understood. An eldritch quality was bound to it.

Harrow looked from Aggy to Max, unsure if the drinks were even safe to drink. Though, she knew that if Max truly did enjoy the sport of death games, poisoning one's captive would be one of the most uninteresting ways to watch their demise. So, Harrow nodded sharply to Aggy, taking the recommended drink, swirling it under her nose -wondering if drinking anything alcoholic would be smart in general- and took a sip. Surprisingly, she quite enjoyed it. Harrow could not recall the last time she had anything alcoholic. It was a hinderence and a distraction, one she couldnt afford. But in this instance, if these few days were to be her last, she would allow herself at least the comfort of a savory new experience before spending the coming days battling for the fate of her earth.

There was nothing else to say to max…well, nothing that would help her in any way. And yet, knowing this, she couldn’t stop the phrase “You make me sick” from whispering out of her trembling lips. Whether he heard it or not she didn’t know, nor did she think he wasn’t already aware of this. If anything, her disgust for him could potentially fuel the enjoyment he had in seeing them suffer. She took another long drink, swallowing numerous times, downing the rest in almost one gulp.

“So…Aggy, “ Harrow swished the remaining liquid and fruit around slowly, attempting to control a shaking hand, “from which decayed earth is his favorite vintage? Is it yours? Or perhaps -” she starts to laugh a frustrated, almost mad low chuckle - “perhaps you were given the position of eldritch bartender as a reward for saving your planet?” She chuckles harder, turning briefly sorrowful “Is…obliterating an entire planet and absorbing their beverages into his palate part of his pleasure? Or just a perk?...the last thing to remember the Earth by…are just a beverage…” she trails off…mourning whatever planet created the drink slithering down her throat, turning her stomach sour.

Aggy

Aggy answers in the same deadpan monotone he has always kept, your words leaving him unphased.

"Sire's current preferred drink of choice is what he has renamed to 'Honeyed Ambrosia', acquired from Earth-2438. However, our Philanthropic Liege also considers my recommendations for pairings based on his eclectic palette."

"I am from what has been designated Aglarian-8,978,321. Which has been archived as completely as I was able, and is the template with which I apply all other cataloguing efforts for any planet the Prosit visits. I assure you, more than just your beverages will be kept in our archives."

Harrow

"hm...eclectic palette." She places her glass back on the creatures tray with a clang, fearing she might shatter it. Though the breaking of glass seemed to be a part of the festivities, Harrow had no wish to partake in any of it, much less one that would potentially damamge her skin. "That he does."

Harrow wraps her arm's around herself, a heavy sigh heaving from her lips. As Aggy speaks, Harrow listens, though her brow raises quizically at some words.

"More than just our beverages," a pondering pause, "What exactly do you mean by that? If -that is- I am allowed to ask. I don't...want to get you into any kind of trouble." She eye's the blob in what she assumes are its eyes.

Aggy

Aggy's 'gaze' does not falter, and the tray is merely placed inside his body for a moment, his face dissipating for 25 seconds as flashes of light are visible at random intervals within his formless cloud. After 25 seconds the tray moves out of his cloud mass and the glass has been cleaned, and filled with the same drink you previously had.

As this process happens, Aggy's voice still speaks to you.

"My duties within the Prosit are to provide refreshments for anyone who wishes to partake at 'Dive', the bar aboard this ship, as well as cataloguing everything I am able to about every planet the Prosit has visited for recordkeeping purposes. This includes your world. This also includes my world. And every world between them since I've been aboard this ship."

Harrow

It was a long shot, but her eyes perked up when he -it- finished this sentance, a softer more curious glint in them. "Your world? Your world being -i take it- one that survived because you too...won a death game?"

"Tell me Aggy, if you can, what was -is- your world like? Assuming it still exists, or doesn't exist. I'd like to hear about your home and...maybe even what you miss most about it?" Harrow studies the cloud like entity with a contemplative look.

Aggy

Aggy is silent for a moment before answering.

"My homeworld was a lush temperate world, not dissimilar to Earth. Our climate was worsening. We were unable to find a solution to polution caused from combustion of various fuels used to operate our technology. The only solution we had left was to leave our biological forms behind, or be boiled alive by the full force of radiation from our star."

"I am the only one left of my kind. I did not win our event. I was granted time enough to catalogue my world before its destruction, and have continued to do so for every world we visit."

Harrow

"I...do not understand?" Her eyes trail the room for a moment, landing on the still foolhardy figure of Max dancing around the room. Then, after a minute of thought, she turns back to Aggy.

"Why did Max...what possessed him to give your earth this categorical mercy? Give you sanctuary? Why not just let you die off with your world? He seem's to enjoy watching that happen...unless of course your world particularly just had a damn good drink." The last part is said like a joke, but her tone stays stoic.

Aggy

Aggy is silent for a moment, his face unblinking and emotionless, before suddenly his voice begins again.

"I believe there is something you might have misunderstood. My planet did not 'win'. I did not succeed in the competition. I survived, and I am able to disassemble anything I desire from the inside out. In fact, I did so to several others playing in the hope of killing anyone from Order in my game. I did not."

"Further, consideration for whether a planet is 'doomed' or not is not taken into account. Of which, my people were not after our uploading. Only Sapience is considered."

Harrow

"I see." Harrow nod's, processing the information and seeming to finally come to a conclusion she understands. Though the expression on her face twisted in a way that revealed a contempt in said conclusion, she didn't press the matter further.

"Well, I am sorry you had to experience that Aggy, even if it seems you are satisfied with the result of your life, I imagine going through that event wasn't easy for you or your kind." Things were getting heavy. Not so much for the cloud perhaps, but for Harrow, mentally, it definitely was. A change of subject was necessary.

"So-" she clears her throat,"-about tonights 'rooms' that Max spoke of, not that I am in a position where you should trust me after how I spoke of your...friend, but, is there anything you are able to share which may benefit me in the coming days?" She held its gaseous gaze with a serious stare.

Grug

"Amusing dance!" Grug says, happily. "It seems no one else will join us in the dance of the Gods, so let us begin!"

Ami Muscaria

Ami giggles and takes Grug's hand to lead him in swaying with her. "I suppose we have to tell each other what's on our notes at some point, don't we? I... am a little bit embarrassed to reveal my secret," she trails off and lowers her head slightly.

Grug

"Uh-" Grug says. "Grug was hoping for the dance of the gods, but this is alright, Grug supposes. Ah- hm. Grug's secret only makes him sad and ashamed."

Ami Muscaria

"Ahh, I'm sorry to hear that," Ami gently leads Grug in a traditional slow dance, holding one of his hands and placing her free hand on his shoulder. "My secret is a bit sad, to be honest, and I haven't told it to anyone before."

Grug

Grug is an immensely clumsy dancer, but he doesn't seem embarrassed at all. "Ami may go first."

Ami Muscaria

"I... accidentally poisoned someone when I was a child," Ami says with a slight shake in her voice. "It was when I was very young, around five years old. I was at school on the playground with my friend, Kiyomi, just building an imaginary city out of sand. At that time, I didn't have very many spores growing from me yet, and my face was not covered as it is now. My family didn't even know for sure what types of spores I had, but we didn't make a habit of plucking them and eating them or anything like that..." Ami pauses a moment and focuses on the music before continuing. "Well, long story short, Kiyomi was very curious about the spores growing from my back, and I was curious about the vines growing from her skin... they had such beautiful purple flowers on them back then... but anyway, not realizing the potential danger, I let her taste one of my spores and I picked one of her flowers to keep in my hair."

"Kiyomi became very ill, and had to be hospitalized for a short time," Ami continued. "Her vines permanently changed as well, darkening and becoming more thorny for self-defense, and her health never fully recovered... it was traumatic, and that's when I started being ashamed of what I am..."

Grug

"Aaaaaah......" Grug remains dancing, but sort of leans away from Ami. "Now whatever Grug says will sound comparatively silly. And Ami is sure Grug will not die if he does not eat these 'spores'?"

Ami Muscaria

"As long as you don't eat the red and white spores, you should be fine," Ami says, somewhat embarrassed. "However, I mostly have that variety, so be careful if you ever do pick a spore from me."

Grug

Grug remains dancing, now even more clumsily, while simultaneously being stiff. "Grug... will come out with it. Grug does not 'love' his wife. Sure, she is pretty, and Grug loves the children he has had with her, but he has no feelings for Morg. She is... too stupid. She cannot hold intellectual conversation with Grug. And it hurts Grug to feel this way."

Ami Muscaria

Grug

Grug
